</div>
<p>The <b>Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina</b> was the <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">military occupation</a> of the formerly <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romanian</a> regions of <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Northern Bukovina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hertza_region" title="Hertza region">Hertza</a> by the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> during June 28 – July 4, 1940. These regions, with a total area of 50,762 km<sup>2</sup> (19,599 sq mi) and a population of 3,776,309 inhabitants, were subsequently incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-King_2000_91-91_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-King_2000_91-91-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holocaust_Report_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holocaust_Report-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Soviet Union had planned to accomplish the annexation with a full-scale invasion, but the Romanian government, responding to a Soviet ultimatum delivered on June 26, agreed to withdraw from the territories in order to avoid a military conflict. <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>, which had acknowledged the Soviet interest in <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> in a secret protocol to the 1939 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molotov-Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact</a>, had been made aware prior to the planned ultimatum on June 24, but had not informed the Romanian authorities, nor were they willing to provide support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rec2_Bossy_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rec2_Bossy-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Fall of France</a>, a guarantor of Romania's borders, on 22 June, is considered an important factor in the Soviet decision to issue the ultimatum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild77_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild77-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 2, 1940, the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was proclaimed as a <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">constituent republic of the Soviet Union</a>, encompassing most of Bessarabia, as well as a portion of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, an autonomous republic of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian SSR</a> located on the left bank of the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> (now the breakaway <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistrian</a> state). The <a href="/wiki/Hertza_region" title="Hertza region">Hertza region</a>, and the regions inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> majorities (<a href="/wiki/Chernivtsi_Oblast" title="Chernivtsi Oblast">Northern Bukovina</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khotin" title="Khotin">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Budjak" title="Budjak">Southern Bessarabia</a>) were included in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>. The Soviet administration was marked by a series of campaigns of political persecution, including arrests, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_deportations_from_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet deportations from Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">deportations to labour camps</a>, and executions.</p>
<p>In July 1941, Romanian and German troops recaptured Bessarabia during the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">invasion of the Soviet Union</a>. A military administration was established and the region's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> population was either executed on the spot or deported to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transnistria_(World_War_II)" title="Transnistria (World War II)">Transnistria</a>, where further numbers were killed. In August 1944, during the Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_Offensive_(August_1944)" title="Jassy–Kishinev Offensive (August 1944)">Jassy-Kishinev Offensive</a>, the Axis war effort on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a> collapsed. A <a href="/wiki/King_Michael%27s_Coup" title="King Michael's Coup">coup d'état in Romania on 23 August 1944</a> caused the Romanian army to cease resisting the Soviet advance and join the fight against Germany. Soviet forces advanced from Bessarabia into Romania, capturing much of its standing army as POWs and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Romania" title="Soviet occupation of Romania">occupying the country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> On September 12, 1944, Romania signed the Moscow Armistice with the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a>. The Armistice, as well as the subsequent peace treaty of 1947, confirmed the Soviet-Romanian border as it was on January 1, 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bessarabia, Northern Bukovina, and Hertza remained part of the Soviet Union until <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_USSR" title="Dissolution of the USSR">its dissolution</a> in 1991, when they became part of the newly independent states of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_Moldova" title="Declaration of Independence of Moldova">its declaration of independence</a> of August 27, 1991, the government of Moldova condemned the creation of the Moldavian SSR, declaring that it had no legal basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet-Romanian_relations_during_the_interwar_period">Soviet-Romanian relations during the interwar period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Soviet-Romanian relations during the interwar period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greater_Romania.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1270" data-file-width="1744" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Greater_Romania.svg/220px-Greater_Romania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Greater_Romania.svg/330px-Greater_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Greater_Romania.svg/440px-Greater_Romania.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greater_Romania.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Interwar Romania (1920-1940)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Bessarabian question was both political and national in nature. According to the 1897 census, <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>, at the time a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guberniya" title="Guberniya">guberniya</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, had a population that was 47.6% <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a>, 19.6% Ukrainians, 8% Russians, 11.8% Jews, 5.3% Bulgarians, 3.1% Germans, and 2.9% Gagauz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-King_2000_24_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-King_2000_24-10">[10]</a></sup> These figures showed a strong decrease in the proportion of Moldovans/Romanians in comparison to the census of 1817, conducted shortly after the Russian Empire annexed Bessarabia in 1812. According to the data of this census, Moldovans/Romanians represented 86% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The decrease seen in the census of 1897 was due to the settling by the Tsarist authorities of other nationalities in the territory of Bessarabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-King_2000_24_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-King_2000_24-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">1917 Russian Revolution</a>, a National Council was formed in Bessarabia to manage the province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The council, known locally as <i><a href="/wiki/Sfatul_%C8%9A%C4%83rii" title="Sfatul Țării">Sfatul Țării</a></i>, initiated several national and social reforms, and on December 2/15 1917 declared Bessarabia an autonomous republic within the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">Russian Federative Democratic Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_84_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_84-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rumcherod" title="Rumcherod">Rumcherod</a>, a rival council loyal to the <a href="/wiki/Petrograd_Soviet" title="Petrograd Soviet">Petrograd Soviet</a>, was also formed and by late December had gained control over the capital, Chișinău, and proclaimed itself the sole authority over Bessarabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_84_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_84-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> With the consent of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Entente</a>, and, according to the Romanian historiography, on the request of <i>Sfatul Țării</i>, Romanian troops entered Bessarabia in early January, and by February had pushed the Soviets over the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_86_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_86-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitrasca_2002_36_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mitrasca_2002_36-17">[17]</a></sup> Despite later declarations by the Romanian prime minister that the military occupation was made with the consent of the Bessarabian government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> the intervention was met with protest by the locals, notably by <a href="/wiki/Ion_Incule%C8%9B" title="Ion Inculeț">Ion Inculeț</a>, president of <i>Sfatul Țării</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Pantelimon_Erhan" title="Pantelimon Erhan">Pantelimon Erhan</a>, head of the provisional Moldavian executive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The executive even authorised the badly organised Moldavian militia to resist the Romanian advance, although with little success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In the wake of the intervention, Soviet Russia broke off diplomatic relations with Romania and confiscated the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Treasure" title="Romanian Treasure">Romanian Treasure</a>, at the time stored in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> for safekeeping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitrasca_2002_35_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mitrasca_2002_35-21">[21]</a></sup> To calm the situation, the Entente representatives in Iași issued a guarantee that the presence of the Romanian Army was only a temporary military measure for the stabilisation of the front, without further effects on the political life of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitrasca_2002_36_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mitrasca_2002_36-17">[17]</a></sup> In January 1918, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="Ukrainian People's Republic">Ukraine</a> declared its independence from Russia, leaving Bessarabia physically isolated from the Petrograd government, and leading to the declaration of independence of the Moldavian Republic on January 24/February 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitrasca_2002_35_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mitrasca_2002_35-21">[21]</a></sup> Some historians consider that the declaration was made under Romanian pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_86_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_86-16">[16]</a></sup> Following several Soviet protests, on February 20/March 5, the Romanian prime minister, General <a href="/wiki/Alexandru_Averescu" title="Alexandru Averescu">Alexandru Averescu</a>, signed a treaty with the Soviet representative in <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Rakovsky" title="Christian Rakovsky">Christian Rakovsky</a>, which provided that Romanian troops be evacuated from Bessarabia in the following two months in exchange for the repatriation of Romanian POWs held by the Rumcherod.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> After the White Army forced the Soviets to withdraw from Odessa, and the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> agreed to the Romanian annexation of Bessarabia in a secret agreement (part of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Buftea_Peace_Treaty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Buftea Peace Treaty (page does not exist)">Buftea Peace Treaty</a>) on March 5/18,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_86_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_86-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Romanian diplomacy repudiated the treaty, claiming the Soviets were unable to fulfil their obligations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitrasca_2002_36_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mitrasca_2002_36-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 27/April 9, 1918, <i>Sfatul Țării</i> voted for the union of Bessarabia with Romania, conditional upon the fulfilment of an agrarian reform. There were 86 votes for union, 3 votes against union, 36 deputies refrained from voting, and 13 deputies were absent from this session. The vote is regarded as controversial by several historians, including Romanian ones such as Cristina Petrescu and <a href="/wiki/Sorin_Alexandrescu" title="Sorin Alexandrescu">Sorin Alexandrescu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> historian <a href="/wiki/Charles_King_(professor_of_international_affairs)" title="Charles King (professor of international affairs)">Charles King</a>, with Romanian troops already in Chișinău, Romanian planes circling above the meeting hall, and the Romanian prime minister waiting in the foyer, many minority deputies chose simply not to vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> On April 18 <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Chicherin" title="Georgy Chicherin">Georgy Chicherin</a>, the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Soviet_Union)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Soviet Union)">Commissar for Foreign Affairs</a>, sent a note of protest against the incorporation of Bessarabia into Romania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1916, the Entente and neutral Romania signed a secret Convention that stipulated Romania would join the war against the Central Powers in exchange for several territories of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, among them, <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> During the last part of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, national movements of the Romanians and the Ukrainians began to emerge in the province; however, the two movements had conflicting aims, each seeking to unite the province with their national state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Thus, on October 25, 1918, a Ukrainian National Committee, gaining the upper hand in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czernowitz" title="Czernowitz">Czernowitz</a>, declared Northern Bukovina, populated by a Ukrainian majority, part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="West Ukrainian People's Republic">West Ukrainian People's Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livezeanu_2000_58_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Livezeanu_2000_58-29">[29]</a></sup> On October 27, the Romanians followed suit, proclaiming the whole region united with Romania,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and calling in Romanian troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_86_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_86-16">[16]</a></sup> The Romanian intervention quickly established the Romanian Assembly as the dominant force, and on November 28 a Congress of the Romanians, Germans, and Poles voted to unite with Romania. The representatives of the Ukrainian and Jewish populations boycotted the Congress, and the struggle between ethnic factions continued for several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livezeanu_2000_58_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Livezeanu_2000_58-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_civil_war" title="Russian civil war">Russian civil war</a>, the Soviet governments of Ukraine and Russia, prompted by the unrest in Bessarabia due to Romanian occupation, issued a joint ultimatum to Romania on May 1, 1919, demanding its withdrawal from Bessarabia, and the next day, Christian Rakovsky, the Chairman of the Ukrainian Soviet government, issued another ultimatum demanding the withdrawal of Romanian troops from Bukovina as well. The <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> pushed the Romanians over the Dniester, and a <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Bessarabian Soviet Socialist Republic">Besarabian Soviet Republic</a> was proclaimed. The ultimatum also came in the context of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Hungarian Soviet Republic">Hungarian Revolution</a>, with the Soviets hoping to prevent a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Hungarian-Romanian_war_of_1919" title="The Hungarian-Romanian war of 1919">Romanian intervention in Hungary</a>. A large-scale rebellion in Ukraine prevented further Soviet advances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prusin_2010_86_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-Prusin_2010_86-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Soviet Russia would continue its policy of non-recognition of Romanian sovereignty over Bessarabia, which it considered Romanian-occupied territory, until the 1940 events.</p>
<p>During the negotiations pre-dating the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1920)" title="Treaty of Paris (1920)">Treaty of Paris</a>, the United States representative asked for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plebiscite" title="Plebiscite">plebiscite</a> to be held in Bessarabia to decide its future; however, the proposal was rejected by the head of the Romanian delegation, <a href="/wiki/Ion_I._C._Br%C4%83tianu" title="Ion I. C. Brătianu">Ion I. C. Brătianu</a>, who claimed such an undertaking would allow the distribution of Bolshevik propaganda in Bessarabia and Romania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> A plebiscite was also requested at the Peace Conference by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Russians_(Russian_Civil_War)" title="White Russians (Russian Civil War)">White Russians</a>, only to be rejected again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The Soviets would continue to press for a plebiscite during the following decade, only to be dismissed every time by the Romanian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Romanian sovereignty over Bessarabia was <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> recognized by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> in the <i>Bessarabian Treaty</i> signed on October 28, 1920. Soviet Russia and Ukraine promptly notified Romania that they did not recognize the treaty's validity, and did not consider themselves bound by it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Ultimately, Japan failed to ratify the treaty, and thus it never came into force,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> leaving Romania without a valid international act to justify its possession of Bessarabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The United States refused to discuss territorial changes in the former Russian Empire without the participation of a Russian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Thus, it declined to recognize the incorporation of Bessarabia into Romania, and, unlike its position of recognizing the independence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltic_States" title="Baltic States">Baltic States</a>, it insisted that Bessarabia was a territory under Romanian military occupation, and incorporated the Bessarabian emigration quota into the Russian one in 1923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1933, the U.S. government tacitly included the Bessarabian emigration quota into that of Romania, an act considered a <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> recognition by Romanian diplomacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> However, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the U.S. argued it had never recognized Bessarabia's union with Romania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1924, after the failure of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatarbunar_Uprising" title="Tatarbunar Uprising">Tatarbunar Uprising</a>, the Soviet government created a <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> on the left bank of the Dniester river within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>. The Romanian government saw this as a threat and a possible staging ground for a Communist invasion of Romania. Throughout the 1920s, Romania considered itself a pillar in the <i><a href="/wiki/Cordon_sanitaire" title="Cordon sanitaire">cordon sanitaire</a></i> policy of containment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> threat, and avoided direct relations with the Soviet Union.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On August 27, 1928, both Romania and the Soviet Union signed and ratified the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kellogg-Briand_Pact" title="Kellogg-Briand Pact">Kellogg-Briand Pact</a>, renouncing war as an instrument of national policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Following this, on February 9, 1929, the Soviet Union signed a protocol with its western neighbors, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, and Romania, confirming adherence to the terms of the Pact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In signing the Pact, the contracting parties agreed to condemn war as a recourse to solving conflict, to renounce it as an instrument of policy, and that all conflicts and disputes were to be settled only by peaceful means.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> At this time, the Soviet ambassador, <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Litvinov" title="Maxim Litvinov">Maxim Litvinov</a>, made it clear that neither the pact nor the protocol meant renunciation of Soviet rights over the "territories occupied by Romanians".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> On July 3, 1933, amongst others, Romania and the Soviet Union signed the London Convention for the Definition of Aggression, Article II of which defined several forms of aggression: "There shall be recognized as an aggressor that State which shall be the first to have committed one of the following actions: First—a declaration of war on another State. Second—invasion by armed forces of the territory of another State even without a declaration of war. (...)" and "No political, military, economic or other considerations may serve as an excuse or justification for the aggression referred to in Article II."</p>
<p>In January 1932 in Riga, and in September 1932 in Geneva, Soviet-Romanian negotiations were held as a prelude to a non-aggression treaty, and on June 9, 1934, diplomatic relations were established between the two countries. On July 21, 1936, <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Litvinov" title="Maxim Litvinov">Maxim Litvinov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Titulescu" title="Nicolae Titulescu">Nicolae Titulescu</a>, the Soviet and Romanian Ministers of Foreign Affairs, agreed upon a draft of a Mutual Assistance Pact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> It was sometimes interpreted as a non-aggression treaty, that would <i>de facto</i> recognize the existing Soviet-Romanian border. The protocol stipulated that any common Romanian-Soviet action should be pre-approved by France. In negotiating with the Soviets for this agreement, Titulescu was highly criticized by the Romanian far right. The protocol was to be signed in September 1936. However, Titulescu was dismissed in August 1936, leading the Soviet side to declare the previously achieved agreement null and void. Subsequently, no further attempts were made to reach a political rapprochement between Romania and the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Moreover, by 1937, Litvinov and the Soviet press revived the dormant claim over Bessarabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Molotov-Ribbentrop_Pact">The Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2932" data-file-width="2386" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg/200px-MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg/300px-MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg/400px-MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soviet Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov" title="Vyacheslav Molotov">Vyacheslav Molotov</a> signs the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molotov-Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact</a>. Behind him stand (left) German Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Joachim_von_Ribbentrop" title="Joachim von Ribbentrop">Joachim von Ribbentrop</a> and (right) Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On August 23, 1939, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molotov-Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact</a>, a non-aggression treaty that contained an additional secret protocol with maps, in which a demarcation line through Eastern Europe was drawn, dividing it into the German and Soviet interest zones. Bessarabia was among the regions assigned to the Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sphere_of_interest" title="Sphere of interest">sphere of interest</a> by the Pact. Article III of its Secret Additional Protocol states:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>With regard to Southeastern Europe attention is called by the Soviet side to its interest in Bessarabia. The German side declares its complete political disinterestedness in these areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_context_at_the_beginning_of_World_War_II">International context at the beginning of World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: International context at the beginning of World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:249px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_world_war_europe_animation_small.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="257" data-file-width="247" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/19/Second_world_war_europe_animation_small.gif" width="247"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_world_war_europe_animation_small.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Animation of the WWII European Theatre.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Assured by the Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact of Soviet non-interference, Germany started World War II one week later by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland_(1939)" title="Invasion of Poland (1939)">invading Poland</a> from the west on September 1, 1939. The Soviet Union <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">attacked Poland from the east</a> on September 17, and by September 28, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> had fallen. Romanian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Armand_C%C4%83linescu" title="Armand Călinescu">Armand Călinescu</a>, a strong supporter of Poland in its conflict with Germany, was assassinated on September 21 by elements of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Guard" title="Iron Guard">Romanian far right</a> with Nazi support. Romania remained formally neutral in the conflict, but aided Poland by providing access to Allied military supplies from the Black Sea to the Polish border, and also a route for the Polish government and army to withdraw after the defeat. The Polish government also preferred a formally neutral Romania because that ensured the safety from German bombardments of supplies transported through Romanian territory. (<i>See also <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Bridgehead" title="Romanian Bridgehead">Romanian Bridgehead</a>.</i>)</p>
<p>On June 2, 1940, Germany informed the Romanian government that, in order to receive territorial guarantees, Romania should consider negotiations with the Soviet Union.</p>
<p>From June 14–17, 1940, the Soviet Union gave ultimatum notes to, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, and when these ultimata were satisfied, used bases thus gained to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Baltic_States" title="Occupation of Baltic States">occupy these territories</a>.</p>
<p>France's <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">surrender</a> on June 22 and the subsequent British retreat from Europe rendered their assurances of assistance to Romania meaningless.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_military_developments">Political and military developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Political and military developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_preparations">Soviet preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Soviet preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(June 2008)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>By directives OV/583 and OV/584 of the Soviet People Commissariat of Defense, military units of the <a href="/wiki/Odessa_Military_District" title="Odessa Military District">Odessa Military District</a> were ordered into battle-ready state in the spring of 1940. Soviet troops were concentrated along the Romanian border between April 15 and June 10, 1940. In order to coordinate the efforts of the <a href="/wiki/Kiev_Military_District" title="Kiev Military District">Kiev</a> and Odessa military districts in the preparation of action against Romania, the Soviet Army created the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Front_(Soviet_Union)" title="Southern Front (Soviet Union)">Southern Front</a> under General <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Zhukov" title="Georgy Zhukov">Georgy Zhukov</a>. This was composed of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/5th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="5th Army (Soviet Union)">5th</a>, <a href="/wiki/9th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="9th Army (Soviet Union)">9th</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="12th Army (Soviet Union)">12th</a> Armies. The Southern Front had 32 infantry divisions, 2 motorized infantry divisions, 6 cavalry divisions, 11 tank brigades, 3 paratrooper brigades, 30 artillery regiments, and smaller auxiliary units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ioan_Scurtu_2003.2C_pg._327_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ioan_Scurtu_2003.2C_pg._327-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two action plans were devised. The first plan was prepared for the eventuality that Romania would not agree to evacuate Bessarabia and Bukovina. The Soviet 12th Army was to strike southward along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prut_river" title="Prut river">Prut river</a> towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ia%C5%9Fi" title="Iaşi">Iaşi</a>, while the Soviet 9th Army was to strike westwards, south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chi%C5%9Fin%C4%83u" title="Chişinău">Chişinău</a> towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hu%C5%9Fi" title="Huşi">Huşi</a>. The objective of this plan was to surround the Romanian troops in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C4%83l%C5%A3i" title="Bălţi">Bălţi</a>-Iaşi area. The second plan took into consideration the possibility that Romania would agree to Soviet demands and evacuate its military forces. In such a situation, Soviet troops were given the mission to quickly reach the Prut river and oversee the evacuation of Romanian troops. The first plan was taken as the default course of action. Along the portions of the border where the offensive was planned to take place, the Soviets prepared at least a triple superiority of men and materiel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ioan_Scurtu_2003.2C_pg._327_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ioan_Scurtu_2003.2C_pg._327-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_ultimatum">Soviet ultimatum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Soviet ultimatum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On June 26, 1940, at 22:00, Soviet People's Commissar <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov" title="Vyacheslav Molotov">Vyacheslav Molotov</a> presented an <a href="/wiki/Ultimatum" title="Ultimatum">ultimatum</a> note to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_Davidescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gheorghe Davidescu (page does not exist)">Gheorghe Davidescu</a>, Romanian ambassador to Moscow, in which the Soviet Union demanded the evacuation of the Romanian military and civil administration from <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> and the northern part of <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The Soviets stressed their sense of urgency: "Now that the military weakness of the USSR is a thing of past, and the international situation that was created requires the rapid solution of the items inherited from the past, in order to fix the basis of a solid peace between countries (...)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultimatum_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-ultimatum-53">[53]</a></sup> The German Minister of Foreign Affairs, <a href="/wiki/Joachim_von_Ribbentrop" title="Joachim von Ribbentrop">Joachim von Ribbentrop</a>, was informed by the Soviets of their intentions to send an ultimatum to Romania regarding Bessarabia and Bukovina on June 24, 1940. In the ensuing diplomatic coordination, Ribbentrop mainly expressed concern for the fate of the ethnic Germans in these two provinces, claiming the number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Germans" title="Bessarabian Germans">Germans in Bessarabia</a> to be 100,000, and affirmed that Soviet demands regarding <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a> were new <a class="external autonumber" href="http://ebooks.unibuc.ro/istorie/istorie1918-1940/13-3.htm" rel="nofollow">[2]</a>. He also pointed out that Germany had strong economic interests in the rest of the Romanian territory.<sup class="reference">[<a href="#cite_note-listref-a">a</a>]</sup></p>
<p>The text of the ultimatum note sent to Romania on June 26, 1940, incorrectly stated that Bessarabia was populated mainly by <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>: "[...] centuries-old union of Bessarabia, populated mainly by Ukrainians, with the Ukrainian Soviet Republic". The Soviet government demanded the northern part of Bukovina as a "minor reparation for the enormous loss inflicted on the Soviet Union and Bessarabia's population by <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Bessarabia_with_Romania" title="Union of Bessarabia with Romania">22 years of Romanian reign over Bessarabia</a>", and because its "[...] fate is linked mainly with the Soviet Ukraine by the community of its historical fate, and by the community of language and ethnic composition". Northern Bukovina had some historical connections with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central_Europe)" title="Galicia (Central Europe)">Galicia</a>, annexed by the Soviet Union in 1939 as part of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland_(1939)" title="Soviet invasion of Poland (1939)">invasion of Poland</a>, in the sense that both had previously been part of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> from the second part of the 18th century until 1918. Northern Bukovina was inhabited by a compact Ukrainian population that outnumbered Romanians,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> while Bessarabia was regarded as having a Romanian majority, even though the larger part of the population adopted a "Moldavian" identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the early hours of June 27, <a href="/wiki/Carol_II_of_Romania" title="Carol II of Romania">Carol II</a> had a meeting with his prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Gheorghe_T%C4%83t%C4%83rescu" title="Gheorghe Tătărescu">Gheorghe Tătărescu</a>, and minister for external affairs, <a href="/wiki/Ion_Gigurtu" title="Ion Gigurtu">Ion Gigurtu</a>, after which he summoned the ambassadors of <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Italy_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Italy during World War II">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>. The King communicated his wish to stand against the Soviet Union and asked that their countries influence <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungary_during_World_War_II" title="Hungary during World War II">Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Bulgaria_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Bulgaria during World War II">Bulgaria</a> in the hope of not declaring war against <a href="/wiki/Greater_Romania" title="Greater Romania">Romania</a> in order to reclaim <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dobrudja" title="Dobrudja">Dobrudja</a>. Stating that it would be "in the name of peace" to accede to Soviet demands, the ambassadors urged the King to stand down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the same day, the Romanian government replied, suggesting it would agree to "immediate negotiations on a wide range of questions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> On June 27, a second Soviet ultimatum note put forward a specific time frame, requesting the evacuation of the Romanian government from Bessarabia and northern Bukovina within four days.</p>
<p>On the morning of June 28, 1940, following advice by both Germany and Italy, the Romanian government, led by Gheorghe Tătărescu, under the semi-authoritarian rule of King <a href="/wiki/Carol_II_of_Romania" title="Carol II of Romania">Carol II</a>, agreed to submit to the Soviet demands. Without explanation, the Soviet forces also occupied the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hertza_Region" title="Hertza Region">Hertza Region</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Old_Kingdom" title="Romanian Old Kingdom">Romanian Old Kingdom</a>, which was neither in Bessarabia, nor Bukovina.</p>
<p>The decision to accept the Soviet ultimatum and to commence a "withdrawal" (avoiding the usage of the word <i>to cede</i>) from Bessarabia and northern Bukovina was deliberated upon by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_Crown_Council" title="Romanian Crown Council">Romanian Crown Council</a> during the night of June 27–28, 1940. The second (decisive) vote outcome, according to the journal of King Carol II, was:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Reject the ultimatum</i>: <a href="/wiki/%C8%98tefan_Ciobanu" title="Ștefan Ciobanu">Ștefan Ciobanu</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Silviu_Dragomir&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Silviu Dragomir (page does not exist)">Silviu Dragomir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Iamandi" title="Victor Iamandi">Victor Iamandi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Iorga" title="Nicolae Iorga">Nicolae Iorga</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Traian_Pop&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Traian Pop (page does not exist)">Traian Pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Urd%C4%83reanu" title="Ernest Urdăreanu">Ernest Urdăreanu</a></li>
<li><i>Accept the ultimatum</i>: <a href="/wiki/Petre_Andrei" title="Petre Andrei">Petre Andrei</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constantin_Anghelescu" title="Constantin Anghelescu">Constantin Anghelescu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantin_Argetoianu" title="Constantin Argetoianu">Constantin Argetoianu</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ernest_Ballif&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ernest Ballif (page does not exist)">Ernest Ballif</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aurelian_Bentoiu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aurelian Bentoiu (page does not exist)">Aurelian Bentoiu</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mircea_Cancicov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mircea Cancicov (page does not exist)">Mircea Cancicov</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ioan_Christu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ioan Christu (page does not exist)">Ioan Christu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miti%C8%9B%C4%83_Constantinescu" title="Mitiță Constantinescu">Mitiță Constantinescu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mihail_Ghelmegeanu" title="Mihail Ghelmegeanu">Mihail Ghelmegeanu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ion_Gigurtu" title="Ion Gigurtu">Ion Gigurtu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantin_C._Giurescu" title="Constantin C. Giurescu">Constantin C. Giurescu</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nicolae_Hortolomei&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nicolae Hortolomei (page does not exist)">Nicolae Hortolomei</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ioan_Ilcu%C8%99&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ioan Ilcuș (page does not exist)">Ioan Ilcuș</a> (minister of defence), <a href="/wiki/Ion_Macovei" title="Ion Macovei">Ion Macovei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gheorghe_Mironescu" title="Gheorghe Mironescu">Gheorghe Mironescu</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Radu_Portocal%C4%83&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Radu Portocală (page does not exist)">Radu Portocală</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mihai_Ralea" title="Mihai Ralea">Mihai Ralea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Sl%C4%83vescu" title="Victor Slăvescu">Victor Slăvescu</a>, Gheorghe Tătărescu (prime-minister), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Florea_%C8%9Aenescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Florea Țenescu (page does not exist)">Florea Țenescu</a> (chief of the General Staff of the Army)</li>
<li><i>Abstained</i>: <a href="/wiki/Victor_Antonescu" title="Victor Antonescu">Victor Antonescu</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>During the same night, Carol II also convinced <a href="/wiki/Alexandru_Vaida-Voevod" title="Alexandru Vaida-Voevod">Alexandru Vaida-Voevod</a> to be sworn in as minister. Vaida, along with all of the above, signed the final Crown Council recommendation, in which Carol II ordered the Army to stand down.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanian_withdrawal">Romanian withdrawal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Romanian withdrawal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1270" data-file-width="1744" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg/220px-Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg/330px-Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg/440px-Romania_1930_ethnic_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>

</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
