</tr>
</table>
<p>On June 28, at 9:00, communique no. 25 of the General Staff of the Romanian Army officially announced the contents of the ultimatum to the population, its acceptance by the Romanian government, and the intent to evacuate the army and administration to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prut_River" title="Prut River">Prut River</a>. By 14:00, three key cities — <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chi%C5%9Fin%C4%83u" title="Chişinău">Chişinău</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chernivtsi" title="Chernivtsi">Cernăuți</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi" title="Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi">Cetatea Albă</a> — had to be turned over to the Soviets. The military installations and <a href="/wiki/Casemate" title="Casemate">casemates</a>, built during a 20-year period for the event of a Soviet attack, were relinquished without a fight, the Romanian Army being placed by its command under strict orders not to respond to provocation.</p>
<p>A part of the population left the regions along with the Romanian administration and over 70,000 request for repatriation to Romania were recorded afterwards. According to the April 1941 Romanian census, the total number of refugees from the evacuated territories amounted to 68,953. On the other hand, by early August 1940 between 112,000 and 149,974 people left the other territories of Romania for the Soviet-ruled Bessarabia. This figure comprised mostly natives of the region, but also included <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Romania" title="History of the Jews in Romania">Jews</a> who wanted to escape the officially-endorsed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-semitism" title="Anti-semitism">Anti-semitism</a> in Romania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incorporation_of_the_annexed_territories_into_the_USSR">Incorporation of the annexed territories into the USSR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Incorporation of the annexed territories into the USSR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldavian_SSR" title="Moldavian SSR">Moldavian SSR</a></div>
<p>As Romania agreed to satisfy Soviet territorial demands, the second plan was put into action on the morning of June 28. By June 30, the Red Army reached the border along the Prut river. On July 3, the border was closed completely from the Soviet side.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romania_wwII-de.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="471" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Romania_wwII-de.svg/220px-Romania_wwII-de.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Romania_wwII-de.svg/330px-Romania_wwII-de.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Romania_wwII-de.svg/440px-Romania_wwII-de.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romania_wwII-de.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Romania in 1940 with Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina highlighted in orange-red</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="890" data-file-width="1337" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg/220px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg/330px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg/440px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_44.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Soviet meeting in <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Chișinău</a> on July 4, 1940.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One month after the military occupation, on August 2, 1940, the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was established on the main part of the <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexed</a> territory, while smaller portions were given to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>. Six Bessarabian counties, and small portions of the other three counties, along with parts of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldavian_ASSR" title="Moldavian ASSR">Moldavian ASSR</a> (formerly part of Ukrainian SSR), which was disbanded on that occasion, formed the Moldavian SSR, which became one of 15 union republics of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">USSR</a>. The Soviet governmental commission headed by <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a>, the then Communist Party chief of the Ukrainian SSR, allotted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Bukovina" title="Northern Bukovina">Northern Bukovina</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hertsa_region" title="Hertsa region">Hertsa region</a>, and larger parts of <a href="/wiki/Hotin_County" title="Hotin County">Hotin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismail_County" title="Ismail County">Ismail</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cetatea_Alb%C4%83_County" title="Cetatea Albă County">Cetatea Albă</a> counties to the Ukrainian SSR.</p>
<p>During 1940–1941, political persecution of certain categories of locals took the form of arrests, executions, and <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">deportations to the eastern parts of the Soviet Union</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Alexandru_Usatiuc-Bulg%C4%83r" title="Alexandru Usatiuc-Bulgăr">Alexandru Usatiuc-Bulgăr</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alexandru_Usatiuc-Bulg.C4.83r_1999_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alexandru_Usatiuc-Bulg.C4.83r_1999-59">[59]</a></sup> 32,433 people received a politically motivated sentence, of which 8,360 were sentenced to death, or died during interrogations.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1177" data-file-width="1800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg/220px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg/330px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg/440px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_11.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Refugees after the occupation</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Serious incidents occurred in Northern Bukovina, where attempts by the locals to force the border towards Romania resulted in the Soviet border guards opening fire against unarmed civilians. In one case, at <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A2nt%C3%A2na_Alb%C4%83_massacre" title="Fântâna Albă massacre">Fântâna Albă</a>, this resulted in a massacre. Incidents also took place on the Romania side of the border: at least 300 civilians waiting to leave for Soviet-controlled Bessarabia were shot by the Romanian army in the <a href="/wiki/Gala%C8%9Bi" title="Galați">Galați</a> railway station on June 30, 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>The installation of the Soviet administration was also accompanied by major changes in the economic domain, as medium and large commercial and industrial enterprises were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalisation" title="Nationalisation">nationalised</a>. The Soviet government also instituted a <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">land reform</a>, redistributing 229,752 hectares to 184,715 poor peasant households, and limiting estate size to 20 hectares in the south, and 10 hectares elsewhere. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivisation" title="Collectivisation">collectivisation</a> drive was also started in 1941, however, due to the lack of agricultural machinery, the progress was extremely slow, just 3.7% of the peasant households being included in <a href="/wiki/Kolkhoz" title="Kolkhoz">kolkhozes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sovkhoz" title="Sovkhoz">sovkhozes</a> by midyear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In order to bolster the government's image, a large part of the 1941 budget was directed towards social and cultural needs, with 20% allocated to health services, and 24% to education and literacy campaigns. While the theological institute in Chişinău was closed, six new higher education institutions were created, including a <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">conservatory</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">polytechnic</a>. Furthermore, the salaries of industrial workers and administrative personnel were increased two to three times compared to pre-Soviet levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_reactions">International reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: International reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(June 2008)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Of all regional allies, with which Romania had treaties with military clauses, only <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> replied that it would live up to its treaty obligations by providing support in case of Soviet military aggression.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> from Monday, July 1, 1940,</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>This week Soviet planes began making reconnaissance flights over Bessarabia. Then border clashes were reported all along the Dn[i]estr River. Though the Rumanian Army made a show of resistance for the record, it has no chance of stopping the Soviet without help, and Germany had already acknowledged Soviet's claim to Bessarabia in secret deals last year. Romania had accepted her destiny in the new Europe that Hitler plans. She will also lose Transylvania to Hungary and probably a part of the Dobruja to Bulgaria. (...) Soviet's Sphere. Soviet was preoccupied with consolidating her own position to the east of Hitler's Europe. On the heels of her occupation of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania, those three countries set up left-wing Governments that looked like steppingstones to complete sovietization. (...) Germany took the occupation calmly. Germany's calm was doubtless real, since last year's deals gave Soviet Union a free hand in the Baltic as well as Bessarabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_developments_in_Romania">Political developments in Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political developments in Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1229" data-file-width="1800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg/220px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg/330px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg/440px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A train with refugees</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The territorial concessions of 1940 produced deep sorrow and resentment among Romanians, and hastened the decline in popularity of the regime led by King <a href="/wiki/Carol_II_of_Romania" title="Carol II of Romania">Carol II of Romania</a>. Three days after the annexation, Romania renounced the 1939 Anglo-French guarantee. A new government of <a href="/wiki/Ion_Gigurtu" title="Ion Gigurtu">Ion Gigurtu</a> was sworn in on July, 5th, 1940, which withdrew the country from the League of Nations (July 11, 1940), and announced the desire to join the Axis camp (July 13, 1940). A series of measures taken by Romanian <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Romania" title="Prime Minister of Romania">Prime Minister</a> Ion Gigurtu, including official persecution of Jews inspired by the German <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a> in July and August 1940, failed to sway Germany from awarding <a href="/wiki/Northern_Transylvania" title="Northern Transylvania">Northern Transylvania</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Vienna_Award" title="Second Vienna Award">Second Vienna Award</a> on August 30, 1940.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="768" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg/220px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg/330px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg/440px-Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina_19.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> helping refugees in Romania in a government newsreel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This led to a near uprising in the country. On September 5, King Carol II proposed to General (later Marshal) <a href="/wiki/Ion_Antonescu" title="Ion Antonescu">Ion Antonescu</a>, the chief of the Army, to form a new government. Antonescu's first act was to force the King to abdicate (for the fourth and last time) and flee Romania. An alliance government was formed by Ion Antonescu with remnants of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Guard" title="Iron Guard">Iron Guard</a> Legionary Movement (partly destroyed in 1938; <i>see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Iron_Guard#A_bloody_struggle_for_power" title="The Iron Guard">The Iron Guard#A bloody struggle for power</a></i>), an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Semitic" title="Anti-Semitic">anti-Semitic</a> <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist party</a>, and took power on September 6, 1940. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mihai_I_of_Romania" title="Mihai I of Romania">Mihai</a>, son of Carol II, succeeded him as King of Romania. The country was declared a <a href="/wiki/National_Legionary_State" title="National Legionary State">National Legionary State</a>. Between October 1940 and June 1941, around 550,000 German troops entered Romania. In November, Antonescu signed the Tripartite (Axis) Pact, tying Romania militarily to Germany, Italy, and Japan. In January 1941, the Legionary Movement attempted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legionnaires%27_Rebellion_and_Bucharest_Pogrom" title="Legionnaires' Rebellion and Bucharest Pogrom">a coup</a>, which failed and placed Antonescu firmly in power with the approval of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler" title="Hitler">Hitler</a>. The authoritarian regime of Antonescu (1940–1944) did not restore political parties and elected democracy; it only co-opted several individual civilians in the government.</p>
<p>Overall, the desire to regain the lost territories was the deciding factor leading to the entry of <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> into World War II on the side of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanian_recovery_of_Bessarabia_and_wartime_administration">Romanian recovery of Bessarabia and wartime administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Romanian recovery of Bessarabia and wartime administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Romania" title="Holocaust in Romania">Holocaust in Romania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="871" data-file-width="616" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg/220px-Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg/330px-Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg/440px-Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ordinul_lui_Antonescu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Antonescu's order to the Romanian army to cross the river Prut and liberate Bessarabia from Russian occupation, 22 June 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On June 22, 1941, Romania participated alongside <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> on the side of the Axis Powers in the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">German invasion of the Soviet Union</a>, in order to recover Bessarabia and Bukovina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> This was accomplished by July 26, 1941.</p>
<p>The King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_of_Romania" title="Michael of Romania">Michael of Romania</a>, his mother <a href="/wiki/Helen_of_Greece_and_Denmark" title="Helen of Greece and Denmark">Helen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mihai_Antonescu" title="Mihai Antonescu">Mihai Antonescu</a> joined the opening ceremony of the monumental <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Tower,_Bessarabia" title="Liberation Tower, Bessarabia">Liberation Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ghidighici" title="Ghidighici">Ghidighici</a>, on November 1, 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 27, 1941, despite disagreement from all political parties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Romania's military dictator <a href="/wiki/Ion_Antonescu" title="Ion Antonescu">Ion Antonescu</a> ordered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_Army" title="Romanian Army">Romanian Army</a> to continue the war eastward into proper Soviet territory to fight at <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kharkov" title="Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stalingrad" title="Stalingrad">Stalingrad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>. Between late 1941 and early 1944, Romania occupied and administered the region between the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Bug" title="Southern Bug">Southern Bug</a> rivers, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transnistria_(World_War_II)" title="Transnistria (World War II)">Transnistria</a>, and sent expedition troops to several different areas to support the German advance further into the USSR.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia,_1941.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="540" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia%2C_1941.jpg/220px-Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia%2C_1941.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia%2C_1941.jpg/330px-Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia%2C_1941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia%2C_1941.jpg/440px-Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia%2C_1941.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interdic%C8%9Bia_limbilor_str%C4%83ine_%C3%AEn_Basarabia,_1941.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Military ordinance forbidding use of foreign languages and wearing of "Russian caps" in Bessarabia, 15 November 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the backdrop of increased anti-Semitism in Romania in the late 1930s, the government of Ion Antonescu officially adopted the myth of <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Bolshevism" title="Jewish Bolshevism">Jewish Bolshevism</a>, making Jews responsible for the territorial losses Romania suffered during the summer of 1940. As a results, the government, in agreement with Germany, embarked in a campaign to "cleanse" the recaptured territories by massively deporting and/or killing the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jews_of_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jews of Bukovina (page does not exist)">Jews of Bukovina</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Jews" title="Bessarabian Jews">Bessarabia</a> who did not flee to the interior of the Soviet Union before Romania regained the territory in July 1941. Only in 1941, between 45,000 and 60,000 Jews were killed in Bessarabia and Bukovina by the Romanian and German armies. Surviving Jews were quickly gathered in temporary <a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">ghettos</a> and 154,449 to 170,737 were then deported to Transnistria; only 49,927 of them were still alive on September 16, 1943. Only 19,475 Jews of the regions of Bukovina and of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorohoi_county" title="Dorohoi county">Dorohoi county</a> survived in these territories in 1941-1944 without being deported, most of them in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cern%C4%83u%C8%9Bi" title="Cernăuți">Cernăuți</a>. Romanian gendarmerie (riot police) units also participated, along German troops and local militias, in the destruction of the Jewish community in Transnistria, by murdering between 115,000 and 180,000 local Jews.(<i>See <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Moldova#The_Holocaust" title="History of the Jews in Moldova">History of the Jews in Moldova#The Holocaust</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003,_Russland,_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="800" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003%2C_Russland%2C_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003%2C_Russland%2C_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003%2C_Russland%2C_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003%2C_Russland%2C_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003%2C_Russland%2C_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003%2C_Russland%2C_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F016206-0003,_Russland,_Deportation_von_Juden.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jews being deported to concentration camps by the Romanian Army</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1941-1944, many young male inhabitants of Bessarabia and northern Bukovina were recruited into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_Army" title="Romanian Army">Romanian Army</a>. From February to August 1944, hostilities took place properly in the region, as the Romanians attempted to hold the territory from being overrun by the Soviet Union. In total, during World War II, the Romanian Army has lost 475,070 people on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>, of which 245,388 were <a href="/wiki/Killed_in_action" title="Killed in action">killed in action</a>, disappeared, or died in hospitals or non-battle circumstances, and 229,682 (according to Soviet archival documents) were taken <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>. Of the latter, 187,367 were counted as Romanian POWs in <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> camps (on April 22, 1956, 54,612 were counted as died in captivity, and 132,755 as freshly released), 27,800 were counted as Romanians released by the Front-levels of the Soviet Army, while 14,515 as Moldovans released by the Front-levels of the Soviet Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_Soviet_administration">Restoration of Soviet administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Restoration of Soviet administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="956" data-file-width="1256" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg/250px-RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg/375px-RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg/500px-RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RedArmy19Aug31Dec44.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soviet Operations 19 August to 31 December 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldavian_SSR" title="Moldavian SSR">Moldavian SSR</a></div>
<p>During the first part of 1944, the Soviet Union gradually took over the territory through the <a href="/wiki/Uman%E2%80%93Boto%C8%99ani_Offensive" title="Uman–Botoșani Offensive">Uman–Botoșani</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_Offensive_(August_1944)" title="Jassy–Kishinev Offensive (August 1944)">Jassy-Kishinev offensives</a>. On August 23, 1944, with Soviet troops advancing and the Eastern Front falling within Romania's territory, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Michael_Coup" title="King Michael Coup">coup</a> led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_of_Romania" title="Michael of Romania">King Michael</a>, with support from opposition politicians and the army, deposed the Antonescu dictatorship, ceased military actions against the Allies, and later put Romania's battered armies on their side. In the days immediately after the coup, as Romania's action was unilateral and no armistice had been agreed with the Allied Powers, the Red Army continued to treat the Romanian troops as enemy combatants, while in the confusion, the Romanian troops were not opposing them. As a consequence, the Soviets took a large number of Romanian troops as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/POW" title="POW">prisoners of war</a> with little or no fight. Some of the prisoners were Bessarabian-born. Michael acquiesced to Soviet terms, and Romania was <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Romania" title="Soviet occupation of Romania">occupied by the Soviet Army</a>.</p>
<p>From August 1944 to May 1945, ca. 300,000 people were conscripted into the Soviet Army from Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina, and were sent to fight against Germany in <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, and Czechoslovakia. Some 100,000 were <a href="/wiki/Killed_in_action" title="Killed in action">killed</a>, while some other 100,000 were wounded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1947, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Treaties,_1947" title="Paris Peace Treaties, 1947">Paris Peace Treaties</a>, Romania and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> signed a border treaty, confirming the border fixed in 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Several additional uninhabited islands in the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Delta" title="Danube Delta">Danube Delta</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Snake_Island_(Black_Sea)" title="Snake Island (Black Sea)">Snake Island</a>, not mentioned in the Treaty, were transferred from the Communist Romania to the Soviet Union in 1948.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_cultural_consequences">Social and cultural consequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Social and cultural consequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At the moment of the Soviet occupation, the regions had a total population of 3,776,309 inhabitants. According to Romanian official statistics, this was distributed among the ethnic groups as follows: <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a> (53.49%), <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruthenians" title="Ruthenians">Ruthenians</a> (15.3%), <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (10.34%), <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (7.27%), <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> (4.91%), <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a> (3.31%), others (5.12%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_movements">Population movements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Population movements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360,_Bessarabien,_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="798" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360,_Bessarabien,_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Volksdeutsche resettling after the Soviet occupation of Bessarabia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the Soviet takeover in 1940, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Germans" title="Bessarabian Germans">Bessarabian Germans</a> (82,000) and Bukovinain Germans (40,000-45,000) were repatriated to Germany at the request of Hitler's government. Some of them were forcibly settled by the Nazis in the German-occupied Poland (they preferred proper German regions)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, and had to move again in 1944-1945. The people affected by the resettlement were not persecuted, but they were given no choice to stay or live, and had to change their entire livelihood within weeks or even days.</p>
<p>Up to 70,000 people fled from Bessarabia and northern Bukovina to the rest of Romania on 28 June 1940 and in the following days, most of them returned afterwards in 1941.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, faced with the advancing Soviet troops in 1944, and fearing political repressions or deportations, several hundred thousand people moved westward to the remaining territory of Romania.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deportations_and_political_repression">Deportations and political repression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Deportations and political repression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MD027-11.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="334" height="364" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/MD027-11.jpg/220px-MD027-11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/MD027-11.jpg/330px-MD027-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a0/MD027-11.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MD027-11.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
70 Years since the first Mass deportation of Bessarabians, 1941-2011. Post of Moldova 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Soviet_deportations_from_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet deportations from Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">Soviet deportations from Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">Deportations</a> of locals on grounds of belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">intelligentsia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Kulak" title="Kulak">kulak</a> classes, or of having <a href="/wiki/Anti-Sovietism" title="Anti-Sovietism">anti-Soviet</a> nationalist ideas occurred almost daily throughout 1940-41 and 1944–1950, and with less frequency in 1950-1956. These deportations touched all local ethnic groups: <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, Jews, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_people" title="Gagauz people">Gagauz</a>. Significant deportations happened on three separate occasions: according to Alexandru Usatiuc-Bulgăr,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alexandru_Usatiuc-Bulg.C4.83r_1999_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Alexandru_Usatiuc-Bulg.C4.83r_1999-59">[59]</a></sup> 29,839 people were deported to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> on 13 June 1941. In total, in the first year of Soviet occupation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> no fewer than 86,604 people from Bessarabia, Northern Bukovina, and Hertsa Region suffered political repression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> This number is close to the one calculated by Russian historians following documents in the Moscow archives, of ca. 90,000 people repressed, arrested or deported in the first year of Soviet occupation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The greater part of this figure (53,356) was represented by forced conscription for labour across the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Casu_chapter_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Casu_chapter-75">[75]</a></sup> The classification of such labourers as victims of political repression is however disputed, as the poverty of the locals and the Soviet propaganda are also considered important factors leading to the emigration of the local work force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The arrests continued even after 22 June 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Based on post-war statistics, historian <a href="/wiki/Igor_Ca%C8%99u" title="Igor Cașu">Igor Cașu</a> has shown that Moldovans/Romanians comprised roughly 50 percent of the deportees, with the rest being Jews, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_people" title="Gagauz people">Gagauzes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roma_people" title="Roma people">Roma people</a>. Considering the ethnic make-up of the region, he concludes that pre- and post-war repression was not directed at any specific ethnic or national group, but could be characterised as "genocide" or "crime against humanity". The 1941 deportation targeted "anti-Soviet elements" and comprised former representatives of the Romanian interwar administration (policemen, gendarmes, prison guards, clerks), large land-owners, tradesmen, former officers of the Romanian, Polish and Tsarist armies, and people who had defected the Soviet Union before 1940. <a href="/wiki/Kulak" title="Kulak">Kulaks</a> would only become main targets of repression in the post-war period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Casu_chapter_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-Casu_chapter-75">[75]</a></sup> Before Soviet archives were made accessible, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R._J._Rummel" title="R. J. Rummel">R. J. Rummel</a> had estimated between 1940 and 1941, 200,000 to 300,000 Romanian Bessarabians were persecuted, conscripted into forced labor camps, or deported with the entire family, of whom 18,000 to 57,000 were supposedly killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_persecution">Religious persecution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religious persecution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religious_persecution_during_the_Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Religious persecution during the Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">Religious persecution during the Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina</a></div>
<p>After the installation of the Soviet administration, the religious life in <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> and Northern <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a> underwent a persecution similar to the one in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> between the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_War" title="World War">World Wars</a>. In the first days of occupation, certain population groups welcomed the Soviet power and some of them joined the newly established Soviet <i>nomenklatura</i>, including <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a>, the Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_police" title="Political police">political police</a>. The latter has used these locals to find and arrest numerous priests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mphdr_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-mphdr-80">[80]</a></sup> Other priests were arrested and interrogated by the Soviet NKVD itself, then deported to the interior of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">USSR</a>, and killed. Research on this subject is still at an early stage. As of 2007, the Christian Orthodox church has granted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martyrdom" title="Martyrdom">martyrdom</a> to ca. 50 clergymen who died in the first year of Soviet rule (1940–1941).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mphdr_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-mphdr-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_Soviet_Union">In the Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: In the Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(June 2009)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_historiography" title="Soviet historiography">Soviet historiography</a>, the chain of events that led to the creation of the Moldavian SSR was described as a "liberation of the Moldovan people from a <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Bessarabia_with_Romania" title="Union of Bessarabia with Romania">22-year-old occupation</a> by boyar Romania." During 1940-1989, the Soviet authorities promoted the events of June 28, 1940 as a "liberation", and the day itself was a holiday in the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>.</p>
<p>However, in 2010, the Russian political analyst <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Leonid_Mlecin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Leonid Mlecin (page does not exist)">Leonid Mlecin</a> stated that the term occupation is not adequate, but that "it is more an annexation of a part of the territory of Romania".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-independence_Moldova">Pre-independence Moldova</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Pre-independence Moldova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On June 26–28, 1991, a unique and widely mediated International Conference "Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact and its consequences for Bessarabia" took place in <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Chișinău</a>, gathering renowned historians such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nicholas_Dima&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nicholas Dima (page does not exist)">Nicholas Dima</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kurt_Treptow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kurt Treptow (page does not exist)">Kurt Treptow</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dennis_Diletant&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dennis Diletant (page does not exist)">Dennis Diletant</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Mikelson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Michael Mikelson (page does not exist)">Michael Mikelson</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Bowers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stephen Bowers (page does not exist)">Stephen Bowers</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lowry_Wymann&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lowry Wymann (page does not exist)">Lowry Wymann</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Bruchis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Michael Bruchis (page does not exist)">Michael Bruchis</a>, in addition to Moldovan, Soviet and Romanian historians. An informal <i>Declaration of Chișinău</i> was adopted, according to the which the Pact and its Secret Protocol "constituted the appogeum of collaboration between the Soviet Union an Nazi Germany, and following these agreements, Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina were occupied by the Soviet Army on June 28, 1940 as a result of ulitmative notes addressed to the Romanian government". These acts were given the characteristic of a "pregnant manifestation of imperialist policy of annexion and dictat, a shameless aggression against the sovereignty (...) of neighboring states, members of the League of Nations. The Stalinist aggression constituted a serious breach of the legal norms of behavior of states in international relations, of the obligations assumed under the Briand-Kellog Pact of 1928, and under the London Convention on the Definition of the Agressor of 1933." The declaration stated that "the Pact and the Secret Additional Protocol are legally null <i>ab initio</i>, and their consequences must be eliminated." For the latter, it called for "political solutions that would lead to the elimination of the acts of injustice and abuse committed through the use of force, dictat and annexions, ... [solutions] in full consensus with the principles of the [1975] Final Act of Helsinki, and the [1990] Paris Carta for a new Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On June 28, 1991, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Senate" title="US Senate">US Senate</a> voted a resolution sponsored by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senators</a> <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Helms" title="Jesse Helms">Jesse Helms</a> (R-NC) and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Pressler" title="Larry Pressler">Larry Pressler</a> (R-SD), members of the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_Committee_on_Foreign_Relations" title="Senate Committee on Foreign Relations">Senate Committee on Foreign Relations</a>, which recommended the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Government" title="US Government">US Government</a> to</p>
<ul>
<li>"1. support the right to self-determination of the people of Moldova and Northern Bukovina, occupied by the Soviets, and to draft a decision to this end;</li>
<li>"2. support the future efforts of the Government of Moldova to negotiate, if it desires so, a peaceful reunification of Moldova and northern Bukovina with Romania, as established in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1920)" title="Treaty of Paris (1920)">Treaty of Paris (1920)</a>, respecting the existing norms of international law and principle 1 of the Helsinki Act."</li>
</ul>
<p>In the clauses of this Senate resolution it has been stated among other things that "(...) The armed forces of the Soviet Union invaded the Kingdom of Romania and occupied Eastern Moldova, Norther Bukovina and Hertsa Region. (...) The annexation was prepared beforehand in a Secret Agreement to a Non-Aggression Treaty signed by the Governments of the Soviet Union and the German Reich on August 23, 1939. (...) Between 1940 and 1953 hundreds of thousand of Romanian from Moldova and Northern Bukovina were deported by the USSR to Central Asia and Siberia (...)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Moldova">Modern Moldova</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Modern Moldova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mihai_Ghimpu" title="Mihai Ghimpu">Mihai Ghimpu</a>, interim president of Moldova in 2010 has decreed June 28, 1940, as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Occupation_Day,_Moldova" title="Soviet Occupation Day, Moldova">Soviet Occupation Day</a>. The move was met with disapproval and calls for the decree's revocation inside the ruling coalition, and calls for Ghimpu's resignation among the opposition parties. <a href="/wiki/Dorin_Chirtoac%C4%83" title="Dorin Chirtoacă">Dorin Chirtoacă</a>, mayor of Chişinău and member of the same party as Ghimpu, ordered the erection of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victims_of_Communism_Memorial,_Chi%C5%9Fin%C4%83u" title="Victims of Communism Memorial, Chişinău">memorial stone</a> in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Assembly_Square,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Assembly Square, Chișinău (page does not exist)">National Assembly Square</a>, in front of the cabinet building, where a Lenin monument used to stand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The members of the coalitions argued that the time has not come for such a decree and that it would only help the communists win more votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_of_Moldova" title="Academy of Sciences of Moldova">Academy of Sciences of Moldova</a> declared that "in the view of recent disagreements regarding June 28, 1940 [...] we must take action and inform the public opinion about the academic community views." The Academy declared that: "Archival documents and historical research of international experts shows that the annexation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina was designed and built by Soviet Command as a military occupation of these territories. Ordinance of Interim President Michael Ghimpu reflects, in principle, the historical truth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unimedia.md_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-unimedia.md-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li>On June 30, 2010, <a href="/wiki/First_Filat_Cabinet" title="First Filat Cabinet">First Vlad Filat Cabinet</a> decided to create the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museum_of_Victims_of_Communism" title="Museum of Victims of Communism">Museum of Victims of Communism</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vlad_Filat" title="Vlad Filat">Vlad Filat</a> opened the museum on July 6, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Prior antagonism</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
